# Wow.exe write-primitive RCE audit

Generated by `find_write_primitives.py` postscript. Looks for
functions that write to a pointer argument and are called in
a loop where the destination is computed via `lea reg, [reg*N + imm]`
(scaled-index arithmetic) -- the same shape as the documented
MSG_BATTLEGROUND_PLAYER_POSITIONS arbitrary-write.

## 1. Write-primitive functions (seeded from CDataStore::GetInt64)

- `CDataStore::GetUInt8` @ `0x0047B340` (size 49 bytes)
- `CDataStore::GetUInt16` @ `0x0047B380` (size 51 bytes)
- `CDataStore::GetUInt32` @ `0x0047B3C0` (size 49 bytes)
- `CDataStore::GetUInt64` @ `0x0047B400` (size 58 bytes)
- `CDataStore::GetFloat` @ `0x0047B440` (size 49 bytes)
- `CDataStore::GetBytes` @ `0x0047B480` (size 224 bytes)

## 2. Sister write-primitive candidates (same-prototype neighbors)

- (none found heuristically; rerun with explicit symbol seeds)

## 3. Call-site audit (LEA scaled-index = danger pattern)

For each call site, we score the surrounding 64 bytes of
machine code:

- **+3** if a `lea reg, [reg*N + imm32]` with N>=2 appears in the
  instruction window (scaled-index destination)
- **+2** if the basic block contains a backward conditional jump
  (loop body)
- **+2** if the same function reads from a global (`mov reg, [imm32]`)
  and uses it as the loop bound (packet-controlled iteration count)

Score >= 5 = same shape as the BG vuln. Score 3-4 = worth a manual
look. Score 0-2 = local-variable destination, safe.
